  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_769a2a3a-c819-4ebe-9b96-5a52cff62ea9'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer939334598577439446">A girl named Rose is riding her new bike near home in Deadwood, South Dakota, when she falls through the earth. She wakes up at the bottom of a square-shaped hole, its walls glowing with intricate carvings.   <span id="freeText939334598577439446" style="display:none">A girl named Rose is riding her new bike near home in Deadwood, South Dakota, when she falls through the earth. She wakes up at the bottom of a square-shaped hole, its walls glowing with intricate carvings. But the firemen who come to save her peer down upon something even stranger: a little girl in the palm of a giant metal hand.<br /><br />Seventeen years later, the mystery of the bizarre artifact remains unsolved - the object's origins, architects, and purpose unknown.<br /><br />But some can never stop searching for answers.<br /><br />Rose Franklin is now a highly trained physicist leading a top-secret team to crack the hand's code. And along with her colleagues, she is being interviewed by a nameless interrogator whose power and purview are as enigmatic as the relic they seek. What's clear is that Rose and her compatriots are on the edge of unravelling history's most perplexing discovery-and finally figuring out what it portends for humanity. But once the pieces of the puzzle are in place, will the result be an instrument of lasting peace or a weapon of mass destruction?</span>
  <a data-text-id="939334598577439446" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

<div id="review_1632342572" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1632342572" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1632342572?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1632342572" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6631709956220647120"><blockquote>
  <i>You have to understand that this flies in the face of everything we know about American civilizations.</i>
</blockquote><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25733990.Sleeping_Giants__Themis_Files___1_' title='Sleeping Giants (Themis Files, #1) by Sylvain Neuvel' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sleeping Giants</a> is being compared to the bestseller and now successful Matt Damon film - <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18007564.The_Martian' title='The Martian by Andy Weir' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Martian</a> - which is misleading, if not entirely inaccurate. <br/><br/>The two books' stories, narrative styles, characters and overall tones are actually very different. Almost all the details about this book do not resemble <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18007564.The_Martian' title='The Martian by Andy Weir' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Martian</a> at all. However, they do share a key similarity. <br/><br/>For me, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18007564.The_Martian' title='The Martian by Andy Weir' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Martian</a> is not</span>
  <span id="freeText6631709956220647120" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>You have to understand that this flies in the face of everything we know about American civilizations.</i>
</blockquote><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25733990.Sleeping_Giants__Themis_Files___1_" title="Sleeping Giants (Themis Files, #1) by Sylvain Neuvel" rel="nofollow noopener">Sleeping Giants</a> is being compared to the bestseller and now successful Matt Damon film - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18007564.The_Martian" title="The Martian by Andy Weir" rel="nofollow noopener">The Martian</a> - which is misleading, if not entirely inaccurate. <br /><br />The two books' stories, narrative styles, characters and overall tones are actually very different. Almost all the details about this book do not resemble <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18007564.The_Martian" title="The Martian by Andy Weir" rel="nofollow noopener">The Martian</a> at all. However, they do share a key similarity. <br /><br />For me, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18007564.The_Martian" title="The Martian by Andy Weir" rel="nofollow noopener">The Martian</a> is not a great book because of the humour, detailed science, or its focus on survival against the odds - it's a great book because <b>it makes you feel tiny</b>. It's a breathtakingly extraordinary concept that we are forced to imagine: being stranded hundreds of thousands of miles away from anyone else. Trapped on a distant planet where pretty much everything can kill you. Putting myself in Mark Watney's shoes was overwhelming, feeling all alone in the vast expanse of space. Having no clue how this situation could possibly end in survival.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25733990.Sleeping_Giants__Themis_Files___1_" title="Sleeping Giants (Themis Files, #1) by Sylvain Neuvel" rel="nofollow noopener">Sleeping Giants</a> gave me a similar feeling. A feeling of wide-eyed wonder at the suggestion of this possibility: the discovery of giant metal body parts deep underground; giant body parts that predate the human technology necessary to create them. The implication being - <b>if humans couldn't possibly have made this giant, who did?</b><br /><br />The story is told through a series of interviews with a nameless interviewer, as well as the occasional journal entry and news article. Unlike <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18007564.The_Martian" title="The Martian by Andy Weir" rel="nofollow noopener">The Martian</a>, this isn't propelled by a single character's humourous narrative, but instead allows us a look at all the people involved in this project - in uncovering the body parts, finding out how they work, what it all means, and trying to keep their sanity as the world becomes more and more insane.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>What I am is very much a function of what I am not. If the “other” is the Muslim world, then I am the Judeo-Christian world. If the other is from thousands of light-years away, I am simply human. Redefine alterity and you can erase boundaries.</i>
</blockquote><br />We see how this discovery and the subsequent revelations affect the world. Imagine what this means for humanity. It is the suggestion that we are not alone and are not the most advanced creatures in the universe. What were these giant body parts created for? Are they a message or a weapon? What does this mean for religions? Is someone out there waiting for us?<br /><br />It is perhaps not as "warm" a sci-fi novel as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18007564.The_Martian" title="The Martian by Andy Weir" rel="nofollow noopener">The Martian</a>. It feels darker, more frightening, giving us less reason to believe the author owes us a happy ending. The ending is haunting and unexpected, paving the way for a sequel that should be equally thought-provoking. I, for one, really want to know what happens next.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6631709956220647120" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1889552538" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1889552538" />
    <a title="Rick Riordan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25375513-rick-riordan"><img alt="Rick Riordan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442449448p2/25375513.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1889552538?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rick Riordan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rick Riordan" href="/user/show/25375513-rick-riordan">Rick Riordan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1889552538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11047093127568856145">This sci-fi novel got a lot of buzz when it came out, and I see why. The basic story: pieces of a gigantic metal robot, thousands of years old, are discovered scattered around the earth, buried deep in the earth or under the sea. Where did they come from? What are they for? A team is assembled in top secrecy to rebuild the robot and figure out how it works. The story is told in a series of interviews -- reports submitted by an anonymous interviewer who is pulling most of the strings behind the p</span>
  <span id="freeText11047093127568856145" style="display:none">This sci-fi novel got a lot of buzz when it came out, and I see why. The basic story: pieces of a gigantic metal robot, thousands of years old, are discovered scattered around the earth, buried deep in the earth or under the sea. Where did they come from? What are they for? A team is assembled in top secrecy to rebuild the robot and figure out how it works. The story is told in a series of interviews -- reports submitted by an anonymous interviewer who is pulling most of the strings behind the project. This narrative structure is very easy to follow and pulls you in nicely. I finished the book in a single day, and I'm not a fast reader. I did think that toward the end, the limits of the transcript format began to show. The storytelling had to use some rather hard-to-believe contortions to report certain information, and by the end, you don't really feel like you've come to know the characters very well. Nevertheless, if you're looking for a quick, engaging sci-fi mystery, this one is a good choice!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11047093127568856145" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1534854624" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1534854624" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1534854624?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2016-shelf">2016-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fanboy-goes-squee">fanboy-goes-squee</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1534854624" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12590256974043413686">Update 2/17/18:<br/><br/>Boy, I keep re-reading this stuff and I never seem to have any problems doing so. I'm still having fun and it's still popcorn fun! <br/><br/>WHAT ARE THE CHANCES?<br/><br/>So why did I re-read? I just got the pre-release of book three, Only Human. It's CALLING TO ME! :)<br/><br/><br/>Update 12/10/16:<br/><br/>Just re-read and what can I say? I still love it. Didn't really miss anything from the first time, but that certainly doesn't matter when I'm just having fun. :)<br/><br/>Robots! ROBOTS!!!! *squeeeeeeeeeeeeee*<br/><br/>And now that I've go</span>
  <span id="freeText12590256974043413686" style="display:none">Update 2/17/18:<br /><br />Boy, I keep re-reading this stuff and I never seem to have any problems doing so. I'm still having fun and it's still popcorn fun! <br /><br />WHAT ARE THE CHANCES?<br /><br />So why did I re-read? I just got the pre-release of book three, Only Human. It's CALLING TO ME! :)<br /><br /><br />Update 12/10/16:<br /><br />Just re-read and what can I say? I still love it. Didn't really miss anything from the first time, but that certainly doesn't matter when I'm just having fun. :)<br /><br />Robots! ROBOTS!!!! *squeeeeeeeeeeeeee*<br /><br />And now that I've got the ARC for the sequel, it's more like *double squeeeeeeeeeeeeeee* :)<br /><br /><br /><br />Old review 2/2/16:<br /><br />A big thank you goes to Netgalley, and I can only ask for an apology for holding off so long before reading this novel. I suppose I figured that anything that would give away such a long lead-time is either playing the really hopeful card or the really cautious one.<br /><br />I'm here on the other side of reading it to say that I had a great time!<br /><br />I do hate blurbs that say misleading things to link an author to other big items like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18007564.The_Martian" title="The Martian by Andy Weir" rel="nofollow noopener">The Martian</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8908.World_War_Z_An_Oral_History_of_the_Zombie_War" title="World War Z An Oral History of the Zombie War by Max Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">World War Z: An Oral History of the Zombie War</a>, and honestly, this novel is really nothing like them.<br /><br />It deserves to stand on its own. And thanks to a little reconstructive surgery, I'm sure it will! ;) Sorry. That's a little inside joke. Read it and I'm sure that'll become crystal clear. :)<br /><br />No, if I really HAD to make a connection with this and some other media, then it's closer to Pacific Rim or Neon Genesis Evangelion than some space adventure or a zombie apocalypse. Indeed, in some ways it's better written than either of those novels. <br /><br />I've had the pleasure to review a few novels with epistolary writing recently, and this one happens to clock in at one of the easiest and interesting, based entirely on transcripts, so it's completely a novel of dialogue. I loved it. <br /><br />Out of all the characters, I think I loved the interviewer best. He or she, whatever the person's name is, has got to have one hell of a head on his or her shoulders. All I can say is, "Bravo on the Long Game!" I wanted to cheer! <br /><br />This is an absolutely delightful and pure SF novel that doesn't dumb down to us, expresses true joy at revealing the nature of the universe, and for the rest of us who are in it for a grand adventure with high stakes and much, much higher stakes to come thanks to the Titans, you're in for a treat.<br /><br />I was never bored. Not even once. I loved the scientific progression that led to the political horrors all the way to the ruthless exploitations. But what really sparked my fire was the quick return to something wonderfully idealistic, even if, or despite its being paraded about as an absolute necessity. <br /><br />There's something delightfully evil about it. <br /><br />If this isn't a brilliant start to a wonderful new SF series, then I'll be a monkey's uncle. I'd read the living hell out of the entire series and chortle all the way, knowing that SF is not dead or dying... it's just preparing for a new and JUST life as a Giant.<br /><br />Is this a Heroic novel? Hell yes. I think that's what we've been missing all these long years. :)<br /><br />Wonder and heroism and a nice handful of mythology to boot. <br /><br />Read this. Read it, everyone. We need more stories like this on the market. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="12590256974043413686" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=robots">robots</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=aliens">aliens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=painful">painful</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=tell-than-show">tell-than-show</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1420121577" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16831615201430822208"><strong>In my humble opinion, this book was 320 pages of info dump. <em>The Martian</em> style except somehow more... overwhelming.</strong><br/><br/>Please don't get me wrong, I am not new to this kind of format. Like <em>World War Z</em> and <em>Illuminae</em> (Amie Kaufman and Jay Kristoff), the story of <em>Sleeping Giants</em> is told in the form of interviews conducted by a mysterious, nameless person who seems to have a lots and lots and lots of power as well as in the form of oral diary entries. I loved it when it was used in WWZ and Illuminae becau</span>
  <span id="freeText16831615201430822208" style="display:none"><strong>In my humble opinion, this book was 320 pages of info dump. <em>The Martian</em> style except somehow more... overwhelming.</strong><br /><br />Please don't get me wrong, I am not new to this kind of format. Like <em>World War Z</em> and <em>Illuminae</em> (Amie Kaufman and Jay Kristoff), the story of <em>Sleeping Giants</em> is told in the form of interviews conducted by a mysterious, nameless person who seems to have a lots and lots and lots of power as well as in the form of oral diary entries. I loved it when it was used in WWZ and Illuminae because despite it being quite straight-forward and in the form of documentaries, these books were still able to touch me on an emotional and personal level. <strong>They showed many perspectives and angles about a particular, seemingly-but-absolutely dreadful situation, and they made me <em>care - </em>care about the characters, care about the outcome, care about how they would cope with their trials and tribulations.</strong><br /><br /><em>Sleeping Giants</em> made me feel... indifferent, at best.<br /><br />Here's the thing: the premise is fantastic. I love the idea of aliens having visited the Earth thousands of years ago, back to that time we were still grunting and snorting to each other in order to communicate, and having left this gigantic monstrosity of a robot for us to find when we have progressed and evolved enough. In paper, that really sounds intriguing. Think of all the political drama that can come out of this! Think of all the philosophical, moral, ethical discussions! The drama! The panic and the riot and the coming together of mankind as they realize its potential as a defensive manuever against extraterrestrial forces! In an ideal world, I would have loved this to pieces and I would have paraded this all over my street saying, "Science fiction fans, come get your mama!"<br /><br /><strong>But alas, it is not an ideal world, and this book lacked the emotional pull needed for me to completely and deeply immerse myself in it.</strong><br /><br /><em>
  <strong>1.) Nameless interviewer. </strong>
</em><br /><br />80% of the book is comprised of interviews with a cast of characters. There's Kara Resnik, a well-trained pilot. There's Ryan Mitchell, her co-pilot; Rose Franklin, a motherly figure who leads the project  of finding all the robotic parts, putting them together again, and finding out what it can do; Vincent Couture, an introvert linguist who hails from Quebec, among others. The anonymous interviewer is connected with all of them, yet we don't find anything at all about him. He's their <em>Daddy Long Legs</em>, funding their research and making sure everything is going smoothly, taking care of "problems" - people or otherwise - as how you would expect an ultra rich guy would take car of them. But... what else? We see the story through his interviews, and we get to "know more" about the characters through his questions, and then that's it? He was definitely a pragmatist, and he was definitely very objective in his questions. "What did this scenario make you feel (even though I already know about it but we'll need to repeat it again just so our beautiful readers here are aware)? What happened to you when this thingy happened (even though I already know about it and we're just wasting our time here reminscing about it?)" Non-verbatim, but you get the picture.<br /><br /><em>
  <strong>2.) Telling than Showing</strong>
</em><br /><br />And then there's the problem. Because of these questions, we are forced into reading a narrative that is 100% telling than showing. "I was doing this, I was doing that, I felt this, I felt that, I didn't like this, etc. etc." It was absolutely dreadful to know that these people were experiencing these things and yet *I* couldn't feel them. I don't know, maybe because of the format it was hard to do so? Maybe because it was just so limited and there's no other way of showing them otherwise? But then, how did World War Z and Illuminae do it amazingly? T<strong>here's also the problem that things would happen in this book, but we would never, ever, EVER see them happening. We're only told that it happened post-situation, when the interviewer is asking them to tell us about their <em>feeeewings</em>. </strong>It was hard to just <em>care </em>when I was never with them when that happened, when I never felt the adrenaline or the tension that they experienced that would make me <em>relate</em> to what they were doing.<br /><br /><em>
  <strong>3.) THE SCIENCE MADNESSSSSS</strong>
</em><br /><br />Now, let's draw a line here: I love science. I love talking about aliens. I find space and the universe and everything that is in it fascinating. If I could, I would love to die floating in the vastness of empty space. But the science here made me cringe. There were just so much that it became overwhelming. The process of how to get the robot pieces? EXPLAINED IN DETAIL. The process of how they are trying to get the robot to work, all the theory and the steps? EXPLAINED IN DETAIL. The process of how they plan to do this and that, and then this and then that? EXPLAINED IN DETAIL THAT IT HAS BECOME PAINFUL. <strong>I get the need for science to be incorporated but it alienated the reader in me so much because so much of it were jargon. So many big words, and none of them resounded with me.</strong> Maybe I'm just stupid? Maybe I'm just not the target audience? But I DO love science, and I love it when it weaves together with the character's personal lives, so maybe it's just the book being a huge-ass info-dump?<br /><br />In conclusion, I'm actually very sad that I didn't like this book more. The ending was interesting, if not a little too "positive" for me to take seriously. But these three factors up there? They totally ruined my reading experience. The only reason I plowed on was because of obligation. I may still check out the next book though seeing as this is a series, in hopes that the narrative in that one will be a lot more personal and emotional than distant. However, if you're the type of person who is a science geek and just want to get your science mood on with or without the emotional touch, maybe this will appeal to you.<br /><br /><br /><b>FOLLOW ME ALL OVER THE INTERWEBZ!</b><br /><a href="Http://thesocialpotato.maryfaye.net" rel="nofollow noopener">The Social Potato</a> | <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Xpresso Reads</a> | <a href="http://notsoliterary.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Not So Literary</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/user/dsocialpotatoreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://twitter.com/kawaiileena" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/fayemat" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/TheSocialPotatoReviews?ref=hl" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="http://ask.fm/fayelapatata" rel="nofollow noopener">Ask.fm</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16831615201430822208" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2421467415" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2421467415" />
    <a title="High Lady of The Night Court" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court"><img alt="High Lady of The Night Court" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556501727p2/62560505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2421467415?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="High Lady of The Night Court" class="user" itemprop="url" name="High Lady of The Night Court" href="/user/show/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court">High Lady of The Night Court</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court?shelf=science-fiction-read">science-fiction-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2421467415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16487520742416066758">This book is a work of art. <br/><br/>Even though it was written in interviews, journal entries, articles and transcripts, the details were never once left out and there was not a single moment when a certain interview felt detached from the rest of the book, which is extraordinary. All the files merged together very well and once you finish reading a chapter, the part of the story revealed in that chapter adds to everything you already know and forms a steady timeline of events which is amazing. <br/><br/>It was p</span>
  <span id="freeText16487520742416066758" style="display:none">This book is a work of art. <br /><br />Even though it was written in interviews, journal entries, articles and transcripts, the details were never once left out and there was not a single moment when a certain interview felt detached from the rest of the book, which is extraordinary. All the files merged together very well and once you finish reading a chapter, the part of the story revealed in that chapter adds to everything you already know and forms a steady timeline of events which is amazing. <br /><br />It was put together incredibly well, the amount of planning that must have gone into this book is mindblowing. The book is was very original and even though it was a new, the concept, the details, the facts, the science, and the characters were very well thought out. The amount of research that must have been done is tremendous. <br />It is definitely very intriguing and kept me on my toes through its entirety. The fact that the story is narrated in interviews makes it all the more interesting because we don’t know what happened in the time between the previous interview and the interview you are reading till you get to the core of the interview you’re currently reading. It was a very engaging book the amount of theories I personally formulated is crazy. The entire concept was extremely well done and the Sci-Fi aspect of the book was one of the best I have read so far. <br /><br />The story maintains its mystery throughout the book and even when the book finished it still feels like an enigma because no matter how much you read there always seems to be more to know. The integral concept of the book was carried out through the book very well and I hope it continues to do so in the rest of the series.<br /><br />A young girl named Rose Franklin falls into a giant metal hand when she was young. And now Dr. Rose Franklin has been put in charge of finding out what the hand is and finding the rest of the parts to what will be a metal giant. Now, nobody knows what this is, how it got here, or even what we’re supposed to do with it. We can only hope that the giant is not a weapon that will lead to mass destruction.<br /><br />The best part of the story, at least in my opinion, is the interviewer. We don’t know who the interviewer is and neither does anyone in the book. He maintains his anonymity throughout the book. He seems to have an extraordinary amount of power, not like magic, but in the sense that he has what seems to be an endless amount of connections in places of power. No matter where the book goes, the fact that the giant could be the strongest weapon known to mankind doesn’t seem to bother me as much as WHO IS THE INTERVIEWER?! It’s constantly nagging me in the back of my head and if I don’t find out soon I’m going to go mad. <br /><br />The book is written very well and doesn’t lose sight of the plot. The science fiction concept is written to the point of perfection. Each of the characters play a major role in the story and I love each of them for what they bring into the story. The cover is beautiful in it’s simplicity and the title matches the concept flawlessly. I can’t wait to see where this story is going to take me, I rate this book 5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16487520742416066758" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2281112722">
  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_1414091425" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1414091425" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1414091425?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1414091425" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15409665036569933289">Man, I loved this SF novel! The sequel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30134847.Waking_Gods__Themis_Files___2_' title='Waking Gods (Themis Files, #2) by Sylvain Neuvel' rel='nofollow noopener'>Waking Gods</a>, was published at the beginning of April 2017, and the last book in this series is being published this spring.<br/><br/>Final review, first posted on <a href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantasy Literature</a>:<br/><br/>I first read <i>Sleeping Giants</i> six months ago and was immediately sucked into its world. I stayed up far too late reading it, finishing it the next day when I really should have been working. History repeats itself: When it came time to write this review, I thought I would take a quick gla</span>
  <span id="freeText15409665036569933289" style="display:none">Man, I loved this SF novel! The sequel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30134847.Waking_Gods__Themis_Files___2_" title="Waking Gods (Themis Files, #2) by Sylvain Neuvel" rel="nofollow noopener">Waking Gods</a>, was published at the beginning of April 2017, and the last book in this series is being published this spring.<br /><br />Final review, first posted on <a href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantasy Literature</a>:<br /><br />I first read <i>Sleeping Giants</i> six months ago and was immediately sucked into its world. I stayed up far too late reading it, finishing it the next day when I really should have been working. History repeats itself: When it came time to write this review, I thought I would take a quick glance through this novel, reading a few pages here and there to remind myself of the important plot points. Instead I read the entire book again, in one sitting, staying up until past 2:00 a.m. Clearly <i>Sleeping Giants</i> is literary crack and I had best stay away from it when any other duty ― or my bed ― is calling.<br /><br /><i>Sleeping Giants</i> takes several ingredients that always appeal to me ― geeky science, governmental conspiracies, a master planner with ice water in his veins, intelligent characters, and dry humor ― and folds them into a mystery about a very strange artifact. The story is told through a series of recorded interviews and journal entries and the like. It's been done before, but I thought the format lent itself well to the plot. We get to know the characters through their own words. Intriguingly, the “files” that make up the chapters often skip over several numbers at a time (e.g., File No. 17 is followed by File No. 31), increasing the sense of reality by implying how much backstory remains untold.<br /><br />Rose Franklin, riding her bike on her eleventh birthday, falls into a fifty-foot deep hole that suddenly appears in her path. When she comes to the next morning, she is lying on a twenty-three foot long metal hand at the bottom of a perfectly square hole, as big as a house, with bright turquoise light shining from unreadable symbols carved in the walls around her.<br /><br />Twenty years later, Rose, now a senior scientist at the University of Chicago, is placed in charge of a team researching the nature of the hand and the symbols on the wall panels. Carbon dating shows the hand to be between five and six thousand years old, and linguists have never been able to interpret any of the symbols (which are inexplicably still glowing). The hand and writing have baffled scientists for years. But suddenly it occurs to Rose: What triggered the sudden appearance of the hand? Surely there must be other metal body parts to go with the hand, and can we cause them to appear as well? As she figures out the answer, the team ― and this novel ― are off and running: various immense pieces of the artifact are extracted (often from other countries, which causes some political upheaval) and put together; some mysteries are solved, only to give rise, in Hydra-like fashion, to many more.<br /><br />Their mysterious handler begins to bring in key new members of the team, with Dr. Franklin as the head and heart of it. Kara Resnik, the hotshot helicopter pilot, who is both incredibly stubborn and irascible but also funny and vulnerable, was my favorite, but each team member is a distinct individual with their own personality quirks and flaws. The key players are Victor Couture, a brilliant French Canadian linguist; Ryan Mitchell, Kara’s co-pilot who is variously compared to Captain America and an underwear model by other characters; and Alyssa Papantoniou, a geneticist with a stammer and a desire to be in charge. Even the nameless handler, whom we get to know only through his interviews of other characters, develops as a character. He appears extremely cold-blooded, though with a sardonic sense of humor:<blockquote>―<b>I read his file. I believe he is more resilient than you give him credit for.</b><br />―You rea … He has a file?<br />―<b>Your hairdresser has a file and you see him once a month. Vincent Couture is a foreign national on US soil, with direct access to top-secret-level information on a daily basis. He has several files, very large ones.</b><br />―You have a file on my hairdresser?<br />―<b>Yes. He really needs to file his taxes.</b></blockquote>But, though he never ceases weaving his plans and pulling the strings of others, he gradually becomes more sympathetic and understandable.<br /><br /><i>Sleeping Giants</i> has just the right amount of hard science, enough technical and scientific details to satisfy the geek in me, but it never goes overboard (like, say, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22816087.Seveneves" title="Seveneves by Neal Stephenson" rel="nofollow noopener">Seveneves</a>), and it’s infused with delightfully imaginative developments. In the cold light of day I have a few quibbles with the science parts, particularly toward the end of the novel. In particular, I have issues with <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the practicality of backwards-bending knees in a two-legged humanoid being, and how these or any other alien beings could interbreed with humans many millennia ago <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I realize the latter is a time-honored SF trope, but still! However, these are relatively minor nitpicks.<br /><br />What raises <i>Sleeping Giants</i> to the 5-star level for me is that it’s not just a grand, imaginative SF adventure that inspires a sense of wonder in me, but it also raises some deeper questions. Several characters ask themselves about the cost of their project in human lives. Rose Franklin, in particular, has an even longer perspective:<blockquote>Am I ready to accept all that may come out of this if it works? It might give us a cure for everything. It might also have the power to kill millions. Do I want that on my conscience? I wish I knew where this journey will take us, but I don’t. All I know is that this is bigger than me, my self-doubt, or any crisis of conscience.</blockquote>More than the question of human cost vs. technological value, some of the characters also recognize the profound change this artifact may bring to humans and our view of ourselves and the universe. As we realize that humanity is not alone, that there are other intelligences out there, the differences between our races, nations, religions and political views become less important, and boundaries are erased.<br /><br /><b>Second read, April 2016:</b> I'm upping my rating to 5 stars after rereading this, which I needed to do so I can write up a more in-depth review this week. Seriously, this is excellent hard SF. Anyone who likes <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18007564.The_Martian" title="The Martian by Andy Weir" rel="nofollow noopener">The Martian</a> will almost certainly love this. I was up until after 2 am last night, reading this in one sitting, <u>and it was a reread</u>. It still totally sucked me in. <br /><br /><b>First read, October 2015:</b> That? Was a blast! I stayed up way too late last night reading it, and finished it today when I really should have been doing Other Stuff.<br /><br />The blurb for this NetGalley book says "<i>World War Z</i> meets <i>The Martian</i>"; I would say more like <i>The Iron Giant</i> meets <i>The Martian</i>, but potatoes/potahtoes (plus I've never read <i>World War Z</i>, so maybe they're right). <br /><br />Anyway, this book takes several ingredients that I really enjoyed -- geeky science, governmental conspiracies, a handler with ice water in his veins, a brilliant linguist and a hot-tempered woman helicopter pilot -- and mixes them into a mystery about a very strange artifact. The story is told through a series of recorded interviews and journal entries and the like. It's been done before, but I thought the format lent itself well to the plot.<br /><br />This won't be released until April 2016, but if you like hard SF and have a NetGalley membership, I highly recommend that you go request a copy of this novel. It was a fun ride. <br /><br />Full review then!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15409665036569933289" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1883791838" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1883791838" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1883791838?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101886700" href="/book/show/25738928-sleeping-giants">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Petrik by: </span>
      Bil
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1883791838" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9875434985094514309"><b>Sleeping Giants is an interesting read for anyone who loves Sci-Fi and mecha or giant robot in their story.</b><br/><br/>This first book in 'Themis Files' Sci-Fi series by Sylvain Neuvel and it began with an 11 years old kid, Rose Franklin falling down through a rabbit hole <i>(not really but still, a hole).</i> After she was saved, turns out that the place she fell upon was on a giant metal hand. The story then fast forward to 17 years later with Rose now leading a top secret team to unravel the origin, mystery and</span>
  <span id="freeText9875434985094514309" style="display:none"><b>Sleeping Giants is an interesting read for anyone who loves Sci-Fi and mecha or giant robot in their story.</b><br /><br />This first book in 'Themis Files' Sci-Fi series by Sylvain Neuvel and it began with an 11 years old kid, Rose Franklin falling down through a rabbit hole <i>(not really but still, a hole).</i> After she was saved, turns out that the place she fell upon was on a giant metal hand. The story then fast forward to 17 years later with Rose now leading a top secret team to unravel the origin, mystery and purpose of the giant robot together with the enigmatic Nameless Interviewer.<br /><br />The story itself took place within our modern world and is filled with mostly conspiracies and politics surrounding the research on this giant robot. Something to praise here is that despite the book being centered on Sci-Fi, there aren’t specifically tons of Science terminology that may confused readers who aren’t well versed in the category. This book is really easy on the science and can be read by everyone. People who loved the anime <b>‘Neon Genesis Evangelion’</b> in particular will definitely enjoy reading this book, there are a lot of similarities between the stories <i>(NGE is obviously darker by far though).</i> In terms of story, my favorite parts will have to be all the intriguing mystery and secrets behind the giant robot mechanism and origin. Plus how the characters dealt with the dilemma they faced between morality and their missions on whether it's better to sacrifice something in the name of the mission or to choose your morality, these all gave good result towards the plot.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I was smart enough to know it was wrong, but not brave enough to stop them.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />Out of all characters in the book, The Nameless Interviewer appeared the most. To progress the plot, almost every chapter contained the interviewer and another character simply talking, whether it’s in the form of an interview or phone call. Yes, almost every single chapter consist of only 2 characters, one of them being The Interviewer and the other, let’s say Rose or a different character.<br /><br /><b>Something you should know about this book is that the entire plot is told in an unconventional way.</b> Rather than telling the story in chapter format, Sylvain replaced them with logs. This means journal entry, experiment/mission log and interviews, it’s pretty much just like a documentary. I came into this book without knowing anything about it and my feeling towards this direction is about half positive and half negative.<br /><br /><b>The positive parts with this direction, it made the plot progression very easy to read.</b> The fact that the prose is really simple, combined with this storytelling method gives a fast paced experience focusing solely on the plot of the book greatly. Considering that the book is more or less only about 300 pages already, Sleeping Giants is a great page turner that you can definitely finish reading quickly.<br /><br /><b>However, the problems with this storytelling method are it was incredibly hard for me to connect and empathize with the characters.</b> This is due to the reason we never get to live inside the characters head because everything is told through dialogue, no narrative and this also means there aren’t any actions to be found. I can’t help but think that this book would actually be better if it’s told in a normal storytelling method.<br /><br />After hearing from several sources that the second book improved in quality significantly and especially after that great ending, I will continue straight to the sequel. <b>Overall, my opinion on Sleeping Giants is that it’s a quick fun read for lover of Sci-Fi and giant robots like Pacific Rim/Neon Genesis Evangelion but it can definitely still be better.</b><br /><br /><i>You can find <a href="http://booknest.eu/reviews/26-pat-reviews/535-sleepinggiants" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> and the rest of my Adult Epic/High fantasy &amp; Sci-Fi reviews at <a href="http://booknest.eu/review/patrick" rel="nofollow noopener">BookNest</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9875434985094514309" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=maybe-its-just-me">maybe-its-just-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=cliffhangrrrr">cliffhangrrrr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=everyone-loved-it-but-me">everyone-loved-it-but-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=i-read-it-wrong">i-read-it-wrong</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=2-stars">2-stars</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1376709783" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8192433084665547668"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461458707ra/18870133.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I may be the black sheep with this one, but ugh. What a letdown. I am not a fan of the interview/journal method of story-telling (and had no idea this was one of those when I requested it from Netgalley), but I still started to get into the story nonetheless. However, by one point, I just lost interest. It pretty much ceased to be a sci-fi novel and just turned into political intrigue and military operations. <br/><br/>If you think you're going to get this cool story about an alien robot - you're not. The</span>
  <span id="freeText8192433084665547668" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461458707ra/18870133.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I may be the black sheep with this one, but ugh. What a letdown. I am not a fan of the interview/journal method of story-telling (and had no idea this was one of those when I requested it from Netgalley), but I still started to get into the story nonetheless. However, by one point, I just lost interest. It pretty much ceased to be a sci-fi novel and just turned into political intrigue and military operations. <br><br>If you think you're going to get this cool story about an alien robot - you're not. The robot is a minor element overall. It's more about the people working on the secret assignment trying to put it together. <br><br>I kept waiting for more with the robot and for more information on who created it. That came in a little bit towards the end, but was just referenced by someone as a legend/story and theory. We never see who made the robot and it's really very sci-fi lite.<br><br>There was some interesting philosophical bits, but considering I think every day about god and aliens and what-ifs and unknowns, this was not all that fresh to me. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1461458707i/18870134.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I hated the name-less interviewer. He was a jerk. I feel he was condescending to everyone and arrogant and dismissive. I liked Kara and Vincent. <br><br>I thought this was going to be much more about the robot and it was more about politics and military ops. So, that is my fault, I guess. I feel really bad for not liking this more since a few of my friends gave this 5 stars and raved about it. :(<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461458707ra/18870135.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's probably just me, not the book. <br><br><i>Thank you Netgalley and publisher for providing a digital copy to read and review!</i><br><br>The part where I started to throw in the towel was when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[they decided to dump the robot in the deep ocean off Puerto Rico. I just was never able to get back into the story after that. :( <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br><br><br> </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1979028521" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1979028521" />
    <a title="Ahmed  Ejaz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53694260-ahmed-ejaz"><img alt="Ahmed  Ejaz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598778737p2/53694260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1979028521?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahmed  Ejaz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahmed  Ejaz" href="/user/show/53694260-ahmed-ejaz">Ahmed  Ejaz</a>
      </span>

        rated it

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53694260-ahmed-ejaz?shelf=2017">2017</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1979028521" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1632948763283612345"><i> I don't like Transformers</i>. So that's for sure I don't like robot giants. From the synopsis, I didn't want to pick up this one. BUT the last paragraph made me to pick up this book at the very instant. Guess why? Because there is written a name of the book which I love more than any other book in the Sci-Fi genre up until now. Of course, The Martian! I can't refuse to read a book which has a touch of The Martian. <br/><br/><i> Sleeping Giants</i> is an amazing debut of Sylvain Neuvel. Loved the idea. Loved the wr</span>
  <span id="freeText1632948763283612345" style="display:none"><i> I don't like Transformers</i>. So that's for sure I don't like robot giants. From the synopsis, I didn't want to pick up this one. BUT the last paragraph made me to pick up this book at the very instant. Guess why? Because there is written a name of the book which I love more than any other book in the Sci-Fi genre up until now. Of course, The Martian! I can't refuse to read a book which has a touch of The Martian. <br><br><i> Sleeping Giants</i> is an amazing debut of Sylvain Neuvel. Loved the idea. Loved the writing. Loved the robot! Yeah, because this book had changed my view of giant robots. I am really happy I have read this book. <br><br><b> <u> OVERVIEW</u></b><br>The hand of a giant robot is found by Rose Franklin when she is 11 years old. That gigantic hand is not the thing which can be understood by the people of that time. But after 17 years, as a professional physicist, Rose begins a research on that hand. There is the mystery man who is all powerful, helps her in the research. They search almost the entire plant Earth and find all the parts of a giant robot. This robot is the most powerful thing the mankind have ever seen. They try to understand its functions. But there is a threat of global conflict. Why? Because some nations want to take control of it. <br><br><br><br>As I read this book for The Martian, I would love to make a comparison between them. Hope you guys won't mind.<br><br>=&gt; In the matter of Characters, this book is pretty much like The Martian. In both books, almost all the characters are dull. At all. But in The Martian, protagonist is amazing. Sort of humorous. In Sleeping Giants, we don't a particular protagonist.<br><br>=&gt; The very thing which I didn't like in Sleeping Giants is that this book has files rather than chapters. File numbers are irritating. Can't be understood.<br>For example, one moment you are reading a file number 4 then next moment you will be reading 7. In the file number 7, we wouldn't get to know what had happened in between.<br>In this thing, The Martian is wayy better. It skips the logs but at least it tells us what has happened in the logs which are skipped. <br><br><br><b> THINGS I LIKED</b><br>=&gt; Great part of the book was told in the form of interviews which increased the pace of this book. Enjoyed the interviews. Especially the interviewer was amazing. Even though I didn’t get to know pretty much of him. Not even his name. But still I enjoyed reading him. He was the best character in this book.<br><br>=&gt; The way by which they found the body parts of giant robot was amazing. Sort of unique. <br><br>=&gt; The way they understood the language written on panels of robot was very logical. Pretty much acceptable. <br><br>=&gt; This book was also trying to convey the message of universal brotherhood. Good.<blockquote> <b> <i> No one really wants to fight, but no one wants to be the one to back off either </i></b>
</blockquote>Epilogue was:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1492282339ra/22502000.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>=&gt; There were some action scenes which were also written in interviews. That was not good for me. I would have liked to read them in normal format told from any of characters' POV. Regardless, everything was fine.<br><br><br>As the first book in the series, this was just amazing. There wasn't pretty much action in there. I think I will get that in the next one.<blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I’m just an old man who likes to tell stories. I can’t help it if you’re crazy enough to believe them</i>
  </b>
</blockquote>[Don't think about this quote if you haven't read it. I just wanted to mention it as I liked it.]<br><br>April 25, 2017</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10259033855679084113"><b>5/5 stars </b><br/><br/>You know what's great? <br/>Picking up a book that you had decent expectations for and having that book blow your mind by exceeding those expectations tenfold.<br/><br/>Also, beautiful minimalistic covers are also pretty darn great.<br/><br/>It took me about two chapters to get into this. After prologue I was<i> maybe intrigued</i>. After chapter one I was <i>definitely intrigued, but due to the format I didn't think that I'd relate or feel any feelings towards the characters</i>. Somewhere in the middle of chapter two I wa</span>
  <span id="freeText10259033855679084113" style="display:none"><b>5/5 stars </b><br /><br />You know what's great? <br />Picking up a book that you had decent expectations for and having that book blow your mind by exceeding those expectations tenfold.<br /><br />Also, beautiful minimalistic covers are also pretty darn great.<br /><br />It took me about two chapters to get into this. After prologue I was<i> maybe intrigued</i>. After chapter one I was <i>definitely intrigued, but due to the format I didn't think that I'd relate or feel any feelings towards the characters</i>. Somewhere in the middle of chapter two I was suddenly <i>invested, intrigued and feeling all the feels!</i> So, Sylvain Neuvel, <u>
  <b>bravo. </b>
</u><br /><br />The format is fascinating. It's told in interviews, journal entries, news recordings and scientific reports. Sounds boring? <u>You're wrong</u>! It makes the story so multidimensional that you might feel like you're in the middle of it.<b> You might want to check the view from your window, to make sure that there are no aliens invading earth. Just in case. </b><br /><br />Also, I don't believe in aliens. So, for me to love a book about that topic so much, is definitely saying something. <br /><br />​The characters! Ohh, the characters. <br /><b>Kara Resnik</b> is.... quite a character! Pardon my word repetition. But she really is. She is also my favorite female character. Like probably ever. I don't even have to describe her, if you read the book you will understand Kara from the very first page of her chapters. She doesn't waste any time on petty introductions. <br /><br />Then there's <b>Mister Fun and Fluffy</b>. That isn't his name, but he doesn't have one. So calling him whatever Kara calls him seems sufficient to me. He's quite a mystery. <br /><br />There's <b>Rose</b>. Rose is a driving force of this story. She started it, for better or for worse. <br /><br />And there's <b>the Canadian</b>. He's cocky and arrogant and doesn't spend much time with you in the beginning, but maybe he will warm up to you. And you to him.<br /><br />There's more people involved, but I'm not here to give everything away. I'm here to tell you that this was impossible to put down. This felt like a movie, but also very life like. This is also one of <b>my new favorites</b>. And I'm about to binge the rest of the series. That's all I'm saying. <br /><br />My <a href="http://bookandsword.net " rel="nofollow noopener">WEBSITE</a><br />My <a href="https://www.instagram.com/book_and_sword/" rel="nofollow noopener">INSTAGRAM</a><br />My <a href="https://bookandswordblog.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">WORDPRESS BLOG</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9245645315766648045">3.5 ⭐️<br/><br/>This was definitely different! Set out as a series of interviews and diary entries rather than the usual prose, this book set itself apart from the start.<br/>It took a while to get used to this writing style, and while I'm not sure the style is for me, it didn't deter me entirely from enjoying the story.<br/><br/>A young girl stumbles upon a giant hand, which swiftly becomes an obsession for the US Government and other leading countries. Where did it come from? What is it for? As the quest begins to unc</span>
  <span id="freeText9245645315766648045" style="display:none">3.5 ⭐️<br /><br />This was definitely different! Set out as a series of interviews and diary entries rather than the usual prose, this book set itself apart from the start.<br />It took a while to get used to this writing style, and while I'm not sure the style is for me, it didn't deter me entirely from enjoying the story.<br /><br />A young girl stumbles upon a giant hand, which swiftly becomes an obsession for the US Government and other leading countries. Where did it come from? What is it for? As the quest begins to uncover the rest of the pieces, there is friction between powers. Each piece lies in different territories, different countries, so who truly can say they own what? At times quite political, a lot of the Government drama went over my head, so I just went with it.<br /><br />Overall, very intriguing and certainly not what I was expecting. I will be continuing with this series to find out what happens to the characters, and how much further they come to extra-terrestrial life. <br /></span>

<div id="review_1800478591" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1800478591" />
    <a title="Matthew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew"><img alt="Matthew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464987365p2/16254355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1800478591?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew">Matthew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=political-thrillers">political-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=gr_awards_2016">gr_awards_2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1800478591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8613276818863085290">Found this one because of the Goodreads Choice awards last in 2016. Not sure I would have come across it if it wasn’t for that. It is a pretty decent sci-fi/political intrigue story. Very unique – I cannot say I have read anything else quite like it. Definitely the first book in a series – while it does have a bit of a “stand-alone” climax, I find it very difficult to say that this book would stand on its own.<br/><br/>The format is interviews and diary entries. I am not sure if this sort of thing is for </span>
  <span id="freeText8613276818863085290" style="display:none">Found this one because of the Goodreads Choice awards last in 2016. Not sure I would have come across it if it wasn’t for that. It is a pretty decent sci-fi/political intrigue story. Very unique – I cannot say I have read anything else quite like it. Definitely the first book in a series – while it does have a bit of a “stand-alone” climax, I find it very difficult to say that this book would stand on its own.<br /><br />The format is interviews and diary entries. I am not sure if this sort of thing is for everyone, but I like it quite a bit. I am a “short-chapter/small-paragraph lover”. Not that I don’t like the big ones, but I feel more accomplished when I can tear through a whole bunch of the book on my lunch break – and I felt very accomplished with this one!<br /><br />The characters were interesting to get to know. The dynamic between all of them is very bizarre – which makes sense as the events that brought them together are bizarre. While some of the usual character tropes are there (love triangle specifically comes to mind), it doesn’t take over the story . . . it is more of a sidebar to the bigger picture – and does affect the plot in surprising ways. Also, there is one character who is very mysterious throughout. While that might be frustrating to those who want answers, it will be well appreciated by those who like a dark mystery.<br /><br />I can say I enjoyed this book and plan to read the next . . . I cannot say I know for sure who I would recommend this to. It is kind of sci-fi, kind of political thriller, kind of world-on-the-edge-of-Armageddon. I think if you are thinking of reading this one but you are not too sure, read up on it, check out a few reviews, and be prepared for it to not be for you. But, if you do, I hope you enjoy the ride!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8613276818863085290" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus">Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) </a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus?shelf=science-fiction-new">science-fiction-new</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2331720912" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5975236732238010888">The author used a unique, new way of telling a Sci-Fi story with mostly or even just dialogues that are so witty, dense, coordinated, interlinked and exciting that the story passes perfectly smooth. I, as a great friend of extreme infodump, can´t say how it is possible to transport all the technical elements in an, for Sci-Fi, such unusual way. Even if one isn't so interested in Sci-Fi, simply the great characterization is worth reading it.<br/><br/>An old question is what one person or humankind would do</span>
  <span id="freeText5975236732238010888" style="display:none">The author used a unique, new way of telling a Sci-Fi story with mostly or even just dialogues that are so witty, dense, coordinated, interlinked and exciting that the story passes perfectly smooth. I, as a great friend of extreme infodump, can´t say how it is possible to transport all the technical elements in an, for Sci-Fi, such unusual way. Even if one isn't so interested in Sci-Fi, simply the great characterization is worth reading it.<br /><br />An old question is what one person or humankind would do with artifacts that are found now, in any period of the future, on earth or elsewhere and what implications and possibilities might open up after the discovery regarding the influence on the development of culture and technology. Be it how it influenced us thousands of years ago or how it might change life immediately with, let´s say, immortality, endless energy, all knowledge of the universe and stuff.<br /><br />If the technology is intelligent and conscient, a new way of communication would have to be found to operate the machinery or to simply speak with it. There is also the key to get all the fancy stuff and the tragedy could lie in the bitter irony that we would forever be too stupid to understand, reverse-engineer or just open the artifact. Like cavemen that got a hollow hybrid carbyne-graphene-carbon nanotube ball, cube or little statue those hidden treasures they will never ever be able to use.<br /><br />It´s scary and amazing at the same time because the further and quicker we will explore the universe, the greater the possibility of finding destroyed, forgotten, stolen or lost technological artifacts will become. The first state or company that finds these treasures might, well, dominate all forever with an iron fist or share it with the rest of the human fractions that are spread all over the universe. It depends on one´s attitude and mentality to choose the setting she/he deems more probable. I would certainly suppress you all, full of evil megalomania, but it´s (still) your free choice which setting you like more.<br /><br />Tropes show how literature is conceived and which mixture of elements makes works and genres unique: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Literature/TheThemisFiles">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a><br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=adult">adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1895179967" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer838274616878515300">This was so intriguing! It's dossier style, a collection of interviews and journals from people who have found unexplained objects around the world and find themselves wrapped up in a secret project. I've heard this compared to Illuminae because of the style, and yes, I think fans of Illuminae would enjoy this, but it isn't as much of a production.<br/><br/>I listened to the audiobook and that format fits the interview style VERY well since the book is mostly dialogue. Highly recommend it.<br/><br/>The only thing I</span>
  <span id="freeText838274616878515300" style="display:none">This was so intriguing! It's dossier style, a collection of interviews and journals from people who have found unexplained objects around the world and find themselves wrapped up in a secret project. I've heard this compared to Illuminae because of the style, and yes, I think fans of Illuminae would enjoy this, but it isn't as much of a production.<br /><br />I listened to the audiobook and that format fits the interview style VERY well since the book is mostly dialogue. Highly recommend it.<br /><br />The only thing I didn't like about this book is that it is obviously the first in a series. There was a very quick little twist at the very end that had me like WHOA, but you can definitely tell that this book was just setting up a series. I would have liked more of a climax or story arc, but this was such a compelling mystery and set up that I'm pretty happy with it and can't wait for the next book!</span>
