<div id="review_1703016819" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1703016819" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1703016819?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=adult-fiction">adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=scifi-experiment">scifi-experiment</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1703016819" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17359657633077749507"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468629822i/19730073._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>"This will change the way we think of the world, the way we see ourselves. This will reshape this planet, and we have an opportunity to help steer that change. How many lives is that worth to you?"</i>
</b><br/><br/><b>
  <u>4.5 stars.</u>
</b> Some books are just so quotable, you know? <br/><br/>... Well, <b><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25733990.Sleeping_Giants__Themis_Files___1_' title='Sleeping Giants (Themis Files, #1) by Sylvain Neuvel' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sleeping Giants</a> isn't one of them.</b> <br/><br/>It frustrates me to realize that even though I laughed so hard through my read (I even giggled! The infamy!!), <u>I just can't show you.</u> I mean, I <i>could</i>, but you'd probably think I have a terrible se</span>
  <span id="freeText17359657633077749507" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468629822i/19730073._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>"This will change the way we think of the world, the way we see ourselves. This will reshape this planet, and we have an opportunity to help steer that change. How many lives is that worth to you?"</i>
</b><br><br><b>
  <u>4.5 stars.</u>
</b> Some books are just so quotable, you know? <br><br>... Well, <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25733990.Sleeping_Giants__Themis_Files___1_" title="Sleeping Giants (Themis Files, #1) by Sylvain Neuvel" rel="nofollow noopener">Sleeping Giants</a> isn't one of them.</b> <br><br>It frustrates me to realize that even though I laughed so hard through my read (I even giggled! The infamy!!), <u>I just can't show you.</u> I mean, I <i>could</i>, but you'd probably think I have a terrible sense of humor, and we wouldn't want that, would we? Nameless Prick's deadpan style might need to be savored <i>in context</i>, but I assure you, IT'S FANTASTIC. <br><br><b>But can we talk about the captivating premise, okay?</b> So the story starts when Rose Franklin, a talented physicist, Kara, an US army pilot with an attitude, and Ryan, her co-pilot (no, I don't have an adjective for him), are hired to find the metal body parts of a Giant who may or may not have been created by aliens 600,000 years ago. Those body parts are scattered around the world and only appear with the help of some radioactive materials, because of course. <br><br><b>-I am assuming there will be a point to this fable sometime in the near future.</b> ← <i>See what I meant?</i><br><br>ALRIGHT, I can't tell this story in a compelling way for the life of me. I do know because I tried on my boyfriend and no, he didn't get what was SO FUCKING AMAZING either x-) so you'll have to trust me, and ..... I mean there are thousand of us who happily fell into the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25733990.Sleeping_Giants__Themis_Files___1_" title="Sleeping Giants (Themis Files, #1) by Sylvain Neuvel" rel="nofollow noopener">Sleeping Giants</a>'s hole so we can't be entirely wrong, can we? <br><br>*headset turned on* <i>Ugh but many awful books are given a 4+ rating here on Goodreads sooooooo</i><br> <br>OKAY, NEVER MIND, listen to this : <br><br><b>1)</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25733990.Sleeping_Giants__Themis_Files___1_" title="Sleeping Giants (Themis Files, #1) by Sylvain Neuvel" rel="nofollow noopener">Sleeping Giants</a> is a scifi novel entirely told through interviews and journal entries, and it managed to picture <b>a complex set of relationship dynamics, which I found so very much impressive because <i>hellooooo,</i> that format doesn't exactly scream <i>connection</i>.</b> Yet it worked so damn well, I cared about every one of the characters, including - okay, <i>especially</i> - the nameless manipulative prick who conducted all the interviews and who made me smile so damn much, the arrogant jerk. In the end, none of them is two-dimensional, all of them are <u>layered</u> and have complex <i>motives</i>, I love it. <br><br><b>2)</b> While I haven't read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18007564.The_Martian" title="The Martian by Andy Weir" rel="nofollow noopener">The Martian</a> yet and hence wouldn't be able to compare the two novels, I completely share <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1632342572?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Emily's opinion</a>: <b>what's so fascinating about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25733990.Sleeping_Giants__Themis_Files___1_" title="Sleeping Giants (Themis Files, #1) by Sylvain Neuvel" rel="nofollow noopener">Sleeping Giants</a> is the way it relegates us - humans - to our very tiny place in the universe.</b> And wow, I needed that. Indeed I genuinely believe that sometimes, we need to step <i>back</i> and look at the overall picture - and that the world would be one millions times less fucked-up if we did it more often. Do you know what French News said about Trump's speech in Rihad yesterday? That he was right to simplify the World problems in a Good vs Evil war, <i>because it would make sense to Americans.</i> Forget how demeaning it is for your intelligence, that is simply not true and so infuriating and unfair. By looking to the world through our First World gaze, we are in denial. There's no such thing as a Good Country or a Bad Country as a whole, and <b>perhaps we should remember more often that in the end, we're all flawed individuals. Tiny, tiny humans.</b><br><br><b>3)</b> The ending was exciting enough to make me want to stop everything I was doing and grab the sequel right away.<br><br>► It was so, <i>so</i> good. <b>Why, of course I recommend.</b><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>

<div id="review_2601841767" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2601841767" />
    <a title="Justin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2795921-justin"><img alt="Justin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528849864p2/2795921.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2601841767?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justin" href="/user/show/2795921-justin">Justin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2601841767" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer718724588236640233">Alright, if you’re going to read this one, I highly recommend the audiobook. I started listening to it on a whim because I had a long run to knock out and needed a good distraction. This writing style isn’t for everyone (the whole book is comprised of interviews and journal entries rather than paragraphs and whatnot). The audiobook has several different narrators so it feels more like a fiction podcast rather than someone reading a book to you. <br/><br/>Anyway, the story started really strong for me. A g</span>
  <span id="freeText718724588236640233" style="display:none">Alright, if you’re going to read this one, I highly recommend the audiobook. I started listening to it on a whim because I had a long run to knock out and needed a good distraction. This writing style isn’t for everyone (the whole book is comprised of interviews and journal entries rather than paragraphs and whatnot). The audiobook has several different narrators so it feels more like a fiction podcast rather than someone reading a book to you. <br /><br />Anyway, the story started really strong for me. A girl crashed her bike into a giant hole in the ground that just so happens to have a giant metal hand inside of it. I mean, aren’t you already intrigued? What’s up with this hand? Why’s it there? Are there more metal body parts out there somewhere. <br /><br />Ohhhhh you betcha! From there, the story pans out from that one little tiny town of Deadwood and that big ol’ metal hand, and we zoom out to the US, to the world, to the Milky Way, to the Universe, to the Multiverse, to the Plethoraverse, and beyond! This thing quickly becomes larger-than-life!<br /><br />I have more questions than answers at this point, but this is the first book in a series so I’m sure I’ll figure out more very soon. This felt like a sci-fi version of a Bourne movie. It flies all over the world, into secret locations, into the White House. It introduces a motley crew of characters and a mysterious interviewer than seems to be a pretty big deal. There’s even a love story thrown in so we hit all the genres. We don’t wanna leave out romance and disappoint Nora Roberts. <br /><br />Just a quick, fun read right here, folks. Dive on into it. Check your high-brow literary criticism at the door and just B-movie yourself to death with this one. Find the audiobook if you can, but read it if you can’t. It may still work for you. The audio definitely kicked it up a notch or two for me though. <br /><br />Really looking forward to starting the next book and seeing where this crazy story goes next!<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="718724588236640233" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3664860202383525268" style="display:none">Bonus star 🌟 : The cast of narrators have done a fabulous job. Also,the epilogue had a nice little surprise!😮😀 <br><br>One of those books where the blurb is much more interesting than the actual book.Great concept ….so much potential…Aah what could have been!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518078020ra/25023794.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Story begins with the discovery of a giant metal hand. It’s clear pretty soon, that the technologies used are far superior to anything known to us at present. Not only that, tests show that this hand was buried thousands of years ago. Are we not alone? If we didn’t make it, who did? Is there a far superior alien species visiting us in secrecy? Thus, begins the search of the other parts of this mechanical giant,which might be buried anywhere in the world. And a team consisting of army personnel and scientists is formed. <br><br>The entire story is written in the form of journal entries, mission logs, interview recordings and occasional news articles. There is this mysterious, manipulative, nameless guy who is interviewing everyone involved in the project. There is some interesting bits about the world politics and various government cover-ups. I wish the author had explored the political angle a bit more instead of the forced meaningless romance angles.<br><br>I don’t know if the format is the culprit. But, something is just not right when the epilogue is the only exciting part of the entire book. It was more of telling rather than showing what's happening.There are no dips no peaks . No excitement, no suspense.Just nothing. Shouldn’t the existence or non-existence of aliens be a bit more exciting or eventful?<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518078020ra/25023795.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If the concept intrigues anyone, I highly recommend the audiobook. It has a magnificent cast of narrators. And this format of storytelling is best suited for audio books, in my opinion. I tried the physical copy and every single night I fell asleep after reading just 8-9 pages …without fail. They were not kidding about the 'Sleeping' part in the title :P .<br>I hear that the second part is much much better and the epilogue piqued my curiosity. So, right now, a bit confused whether to continue with the series. We’ll see :)</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8909020215389056002"><b>-	Would you like to clarify your former statement concerning Big Dumb Objects?</b><br/><br/>-	Oh, I see that this review is going to be in the style of <i>Sleeping Giants</i> itself, which is, a series of interviews between an unnamed insufferable smug know-it-all who seems to have more clout than the President of the United and a series of cardboard cutouts.<br/><br/><b>- Cutouts?   <span id="freeText8909020215389056002" style="display:none"><b>-	Would you like to clarify your former statement concerning Big Dumb Objects?</b><br /><br />-	Oh, I see that this review is going to be in the style of <i>Sleeping Giants</i> itself, which is, a series of interviews between an unnamed insufferable smug know-it-all who seems to have more clout than the President of the United and a series of cardboard cutouts.<br /><br /><b>- Cutouts? Rather supercilious of <i>you</i>, I would have said, never mind me.</b><br /><br />-	Well, how about : the Ripley ripoff – she’s from Alien The Movie you know – and the superintelligent geek, and the Mad Scientist – this is not profound characterization, you know. <br /><br /><b>- Mmm, well, okay, but back to the Object.</b><br /><br />-	Okay, well, the Big Dumb Object - it’s an affectionate term for something you find very often in science fiction and I should say that Sleeping Giants is science fiction for people who don’t read science fiction. Think of the monolith in 2001 A Space Odyssey or Rama in Arthur Clarke’s Rendezvous with Rama or Ringworld – anyway, there are dozens of sf stories in which humans discover an Extra Terrestrial Thing and it’s always HUGE, it’s never 3 inches by 4 inches by 6 inches. <br /><br /><b>-	So you’re saying that the 20 stories high robot discovered bit by bit in this novel is one of those.</b><br /><br />-	If you want to create a sense of wonder, have your robot be 20 stories high. That will work every time. <br /><br /><b>-	So, within the confines of its alleged oldfashioned sensibility, then, does this entry-level science fiction novel work or not?</b><br /><br />-	Actual sf writers, if they come across this one, will be gnawing their own lower left arm off in frustration. Their intricate masterpieces sail by unnoticed by the multitude, but everyone falls instantly in love with this johnny-one-note tale.<br /><br /><b>-	It was ever thus, you know. Ben Jonson thought Shakespeare was a bit crap compared to his own stuff.</b><br /><br />-	And the incessant sneeriness of the egomaniac who drives all these interviews gets more than a bit irritating.<br /><br /><b>-	Are you implying anything here?</b><br /><br />-	Oh no, present company excepted. <br /><br /><b>-	Most kind.</b><br /><br />-	But, you know, it was a real fast prawn crackery read. <br /><br /><b>-	?</b><br /><br />-	You know – OMG did I just eat a whole bag? And why, since they're completely tasteless?<br /><br /><b>-	So?</b><br /><br />-	Well, I can see why some readers ladle out the stars, but for this old sf fan from way back, awarding a second star is my good deed for the day, akin to helping a three legged dog across the road.<br /><br /><b>-	!</b></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13113560457793001602">well, that was......interesting<br/><br/>i feel like i just walked out of a sci-fi movie and my brain is still trying to catch up<br/><br/>this book was published in 2016 WHY HAS IT NOT GARNERED MORE HYPE??? (sidenote: how do books get hyped, like is there one person in charge of determining that?? more than one? a collective? a squad of super cool readers that choose which books get hyped and which get pushed to the side?? so many burning questions, so little answers)<br/><br/>but W O W<br/><br/>I think book 1 is just skimming the su</span>
  <span id="freeText13113560457793001602" style="display:none">well, that was......interesting<br /><br />i feel like i just walked out of a sci-fi movie and my brain is still trying to catch up<br /><br />this book was published in 2016 WHY HAS IT NOT GARNERED MORE HYPE??? (sidenote: how do books get hyped, like is there one person in charge of determining that?? more than one? a collective? a squad of super cool readers that choose which books get hyped and which get pushed to the side?? so many burning questions, so little answers)<br /><br />but W O W<br /><br />I think book 1 is just skimming the surface of whats to come, this book contains so much amazing development in characters, plot, the potential the rest of this series has, at this point its really open to anything<br /><br />the concept to me is so fricken cool, im not a science/math girl in ANY sense, i literally just did the mandatory studies for them then nosedived right into english and writing and anything to do with words so i thought i might be to //dumb// to understand all this sciencey stuff BUT ITS EXPLAINED REALLY WELL IN EASY LANGUAGE<br /><br />im so impressed with how the author chose to write this book, its written in an interview format (yes the entire thing) and while some might find it tiring (it can be) i thought it was a really creative way to approach a story that might normally be very info-dumpy <br /><br />^thats like the #1 reason why i typically shy away from sci-fi, usually the authors have a WHOLE LOAD of world building to do so its like LETS DUMP IT ALL ON THEM FROM THE START and im just so not into that bUT THIS WAS A REALLY CREATIVE WAY OF GETTING ALL THE INFORMATION DOWN WITHOUT COMING OFF AS BORING THE READERS TO TEARS <br /><br />i listened to the audiobook and KIDS DO YOURSELF A FAVOUR AND GET IT<br /><br />there's a whole cast and while in the beginning i had a hard time remembering the characters (their first and last names are used quite interchangeably) but you BUILD SUCH A CONNECTION WITH THE CHARACTERS, theyre so <b>real</b> and towards the end i was ready to round them all up and give them cuddles and warm cookies <br /><br />really a fantastic production im so impressed, brb ordering book 2<br /><br />4.5 stars</span>

<div id="review_3104253391" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3104253391" />
    <a title="jaime ⭐️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63531944-jaime"><img alt="jaime ⭐️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577483906p2/63531944.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3104253391?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jaime ⭐️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jaime ⭐️" href="/user/show/63531944-jaime">jaime ⭐️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63531944-jaime?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63531944-jaime?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63531944-jaime?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3104253391" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7852618286529324532">➽ <i>book 4 out of 100</i><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1579041650i/28779328._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Sleeping Giants had me at the prologue. It tells the story of a 10 year old girl who rides her bike into the forest one evening and falls into a crater that is the home of a giant metal hand. Cut to twenty years later and that same girl is now 31 and the leader of a research project that is determined to find the matching body parts to this hand that are hidden all over the world.<br/><br/>This book was an interesting read for me. I’m not the hugest science fiction fan so I felt that a </span>
  <span id="freeText7852618286529324532" style="display:none">➽ <i>book 4 out of 100</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1579041650i/28779328._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sleeping Giants had me at the prologue. It tells the story of a 10 year old girl who rides her bike into the forest one evening and falls into a crater that is the home of a giant metal hand. Cut to twenty years later and that same girl is now 31 and the leader of a research project that is determined to find the matching body parts to this hand that are hidden all over the world.<br><br>This book was an interesting read for me. I’m not the hugest science fiction fan so I felt that a lot of this story was lost on me. It was very heavy on the science, considering it’s told in interview format and through journal entries, and the majority of our characters are scientific researchers very much invested in their work. However, I did spent the majority of the book interested and wanting to know what happened next.<br><br>I personally loved the format. I love when books are somewhat multi-media, so I loved that we got newspaper clippings, journal entries, and interviews. I’ve also heard that the audiobook is full cast, so that’s definitely something worth checking out. I also felt that this format gave the individual characters such strong voices. I didn’t even need to look at the chapter header to understand who was talking in that moment. My personal favourite character was the snarky and sarcastic <b> Kara Resnik, </b>an ex-military pilot. Most of her entires were full of rude comments that were super hilarious.<br><br>I do love that the majority of the characters were female, in what seems like such a usually male-dominated setting. I loved to see women in leadership roles, and taken seriously by the other male characters. The fact that they were female and in the military or performing such complex scientific tasks wasn’t discussed at all and I appreciated the normalcy of that. One tiny thing that bothered me however, was the fact that I knew exactly what the female characters looked like and I knew that they were attractive, but I couldn’t picture the male characters at all. I’m nitpicking though, I thought this was actually a rather feminist work.<br><br>The plot of this book moves incredibly fast, which felt somewhat jarring to me. I didn’t love the war aspects of this book, and I preferred to read more about the research project, and the scientists figuring out more about the robot and making guesses about potential alien life form. The middle of the book was probably when I was the most invested and by the time I got to the last 25%, I lost interest.<br><br>I don’t really have much else to say about this book, but it is worth a read. I just think I’m probably not the right audience, as I’m not a huge science fiction fan. I’m glad I read it and stepped out of my comfort zone but I probably won’t pick up the other books in the series.<br><br>❀ buddy read with <a href="https://twitter.com/alkemireads" rel="nofollow noopener">jakob,</a> <a href="https://twitter.com/ALINIVILANON" rel="nofollow noopener">emma,</a>and <a href="https://twitter.com/Courtenie13" rel="nofollow noopener">courtenie</a> ❀<br><br><a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/leoreads" rel="nofollow noopener">youtube</a> ❀ <a href="https://twitter.com/leoreads1" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> ❀ <a href="https://www.instagram.com/jaime.mcdermott/" rel="nofollow noopener">instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7852618286529324532" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1380348270" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1380348270" />
    <a title="Karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7784766-karen"><img alt="Karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1511109914p2/7784766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1380348270?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen" href="/user/show/7784766-karen">Karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7784766-karen?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7784766-karen?shelf=won-from-goodreads">won-from-goodreads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7784766-karen?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1380348270" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer823042296860789704">This was such a fun read. I am sad I read it because NOW I have to wait over a year for the sequel. This had such imagination and I loved the concept. It is a pretty addictive read right from the start. In the beginning a young girl finds a giant hand. This is the first piece of what is actually a metal type of giant. Years later that woman leads a team to find the rest of the parts to put it all together. Told in a series of interviews with an unnamed narrator, this book was an addictive read. </span>
  <span id="freeText823042296860789704" style="display:none">This was such a fun read. I am sad I read it because NOW I have to wait over a year for the sequel. This had such imagination and I loved the concept. It is a pretty addictive read right from the start. In the beginning a young girl finds a giant hand. This is the first piece of what is actually a metal type of giant. Years later that woman leads a team to find the rest of the parts to put it all together. Told in a series of interviews with an unnamed narrator, this book was an addictive read. We meet so many interesting characters and the story takes us all over the world.<br /><br />I have a hard time picking favorites for this book. I loved so much about this story. Although the formatting for this book was different, I had no problem following along. The interviewer’s identity was the most intriguing. At first this person is just talking about the characters, and then they are interacting with each player interview style. As they get more comfortable with him, (or her), we get to know the players more intimately. Each of them has an interesting story to tell. The interviewer’s identity is never revealed, but I quickly came to realized this person knows more than anyone about the machine.<br /><br />Honestly, so much happens in the course of this book. Each piece builds upon itself. To say more would just give the story away. I liked this book too much to spoil it for you. The pacing of this story was nothing short of brilliant. We go all over the world, but the main focus is on the machine, which is incredibly imaginative. It is not as far fetched as some science fiction. Indeed, it was easy to imagine this story in a reality. The politics and bureaucratic bullshit that influence the story were very easy to relate to in these times.<br /><br />This is fantastical science fiction that I want everyone to read. I cannot wait for the sequel. I highly recommend this!</span>
  <a data-text-id="823042296860789704" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('CzIiwT4Z6yeqoizBr05jNVaSWvsUe4ODn92VubOt95gaQFC7XT2LumMCgt5vzCimz6m5V2jNgb6zCVb1Fz73Ow==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('D5MawPLgtGlQYPjsM/M285mEo6bUXNT90z4RoBIdkAse4Wi6kcTU9JnAVvPzcX1gAL9ACqjq1sD/6tLsto6QqA==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14699117055597511013">Sylvain Neuvel dropped out of high school at age 15. Along the way, he has been a journalist, worked in soil decontamination, sold ice cream in California, and peddled furniture across Canada. He received a Ph.D. in linguistics from the University of Chicago. He taught linguistics in India, and worked as a software engineer in Montreal. He is also a certified translator, though he wishes he were a</span>
  <span id="freeText14699117055597511013" style="display:none">Sylvain Neuvel dropped out of high school at age 15. Along the way, he has been a journalist, worked in soil decontamination, sold ice cream in California, and peddled furniture across Canada. He received a Ph.D. in linguistics from the University of Chicago. He taught linguistics in India, and worked as a software engineer in Montreal. He is also a certified translator, though he wishes he were an astronaut. He likes to tinker, dabbles in robotics and is somewhat obsessed with Halloween. He absolutely loves toys; his girlfriend would have him believe that he has too many, so he writes about aliens and giant robots as a blatant excuse to build action figures (for his son, of course). </span>
  <a data-text-id="14699117055597511013" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
